<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">List of ATP number 1 ranked singles tennis players</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">This article is about ATP number 1 rankings since 1973. For the all-time list, see <a href="/wiki/World_number_1_male_tennis_player_rankings" title="World number 1 male tennis player rankings">World number 1 male tennis player rankings</a>.</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/ATP_Rankings" title="ATP Rankings">ATP Rankings</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Tennis_Professionals" title="Association of Tennis Professionals">Association of Tennis Professionals</a>' (ATP) merit-based method for determining the rankings in men's <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>. The top-ranked player is the player who, over the previous 52 weeks, has garnered the most ATP ranking points.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Murray_A._US16_(10)_(29236489603).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1564" data-file-width="1055" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Murray_A._US16_%2810%29_%2829236489603%29.jpg/200px-Murray_A._US16_%2810%29_%2829236489603%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Murray_A._US16_%2810%29_%2829236489603%29.jpg/300px-Murray_A._US16_%2810%29_%2829236489603%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Murray_A._US16_%2810%29_%2829236489603%29.jpg/400px-Murray_A._US16_%2810%29_%2829236489603%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Murray_A._US16_(10)_(29236489603).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<center><a href="/wiki/Andy_Murray" title="Andy Murray">Andy Murray</a>, the current world No. 1.</center>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Points are awarded based on how far a player advances in tournaments and the category of those tournaments. The ATP has used a computerized system for determining the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_number_one_male_tennis_player_rankings" title="World number one male tennis player rankings">rankings</a> since 23 August 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Starting in 1979, an updated rankings list is released at the beginning of each week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 1973, 26 men have been ranked number 1 by the ATP,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> of which 17 have been year-end number 1. The current world number one is <a href="/wiki/Andy_Murray" title="Andy Murray">Andy Murray</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranking_method">Ranking method</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_ATP_number_1_ranked_singles_tennis_players&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Ranking method">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since the introduction of the ATP rankings the method used to calculate a player's ranking points has changed several times. As of 2011, the rankings are calculated by totaling the points a player wins in his best eighteen tournaments, subject to certain restrictions. For top players the counting tournaments are the four <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> tournaments, the eight mandatory <a href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour_Masters_1000" title="ATP World Tour Masters 1000">ATP World Tour Masters 1000</a> tournaments, the player's best four eligible <a href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour_500_series" title="ATP World Tour 500 series">ATP World Tour 500 series</a> tournaments (the non-mandatory ATP Masters 1000 event in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo_Masters" title="Monte Carlo Masters">Monte Carlo</a> may be substituted for one of these), and his best two results from <a href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour_250_series" title="ATP World Tour 250 series">ATP World Tour 250 series</a>. Lower-ranked players who are not eligible for some or all of the top tournaments may include additional ATP 500 and ATP 250 events, and also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ATP_Challenger_Series" title="ATP Challenger Series">ATP Challenger Series</a>, and Futures Series tournaments. The ranking points of players who qualify for the year-end <a href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour_Finals" title="ATP World Tour Finals">ATP World Tour Finals</a> also include any points gained at that tournament, increasing their counting tournament total to nineteen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_and_particularities">Records and particularities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_ATP_number_1_ranked_singles_tennis_players&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Records and particularities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a> holds the records for both the most total weeks at number 1 (302) and most consecutive weeks at number 1 (237).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_of_No._1_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_No._1-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pete_Sampras" title="Pete Sampras">Pete Sampras</a> holds the record for the most year-end number 1 (six, all consecutive).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sampras_6_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sampras_6-9">[9]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patrick_Rafter" title="Patrick Rafter">Patrick Rafter</a> spent the fewest weeks at number 1 (one week).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lleyton_Hewitt" title="Lleyton Hewitt">Lleyton Hewitt</a> is both the youngest world number 1 (20 years, 268 days) and youngest year-end number 1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hewitt_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hewitt-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Lendl" title="Ivan Lendl">Ivan Lendl</a> is the oldest year-end number 1 (29 years, 299 days). <a href="/wiki/Andre_Agassi" title="Andre Agassi">Andre Agassi</a> is the oldest number 1 (33 years, 131 days).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Only four players have regained the year end No. 1 ranking, Lendl in 1989, Federer in 2009, Nadal in 2010, and Djokovic in 2014. Only one player regained the year end No. 1 ranking a second time, Nadal in 2013.</p>
<p>Two players, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Lendl" title="Ivan Lendl">Ivan Lendl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_R%C3%ADos" title="Marcelo Ríos">Marcelo Ríos</a>, have reached number 1 without previously having won a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rios_No._1_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rios_No._1-15">[15]</a></sup> Lendl reached number 1 on February 21, 1983, but did not win his first Grand Slam title until the <a href="/wiki/1984_French_Open" title="1984 French Open">1984 French Open</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Rios reached number 1 on March 30, 1998 and is the only number 1 player who never won a Grand Slam singles title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 1973 when the ATP ranking started, there have been twelve years when one player held the top spot for the entire year. In contrast, 1999 had the most number 1 players of any year since the rankings started. There were five players who were number 1 sometime during that year - Sampras, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlos_Moya" title="Carlos Moya">Carlos Moya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Kafelnikov" title="Yevgeny Kafelnikov">Yevgeny Kafelnikov</a>, Agassi and Rafter. John McEnroe held the No. 1 ranking on a record 14 different occasions and Pete Sampras was the only other player to hold it on 10 or more occasions with 11 different stints.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Number_1_ranked_players">Number 1 ranked players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_ATP_number_1_ranked_singles_tennis_players&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Number 1 ranked players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dd><i>The statistics are updated only when the ATP website revises its rankings (usually every Monday morning except when tournament finals are postponed).</i></dd>
</dl>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jimmy_Connors_cropped.jpg"><img alt="A man wearing white clothes swinging a tennis racket" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="320" data-file-width="230" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Jimmy_Connors_cropped.jpg/200px-Jimmy_Connors_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/62/Jimmy_Connors_cropped.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jimmy_Connors_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<center><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Connors" title="Jimmy Connors">Jimmy Connors</a> spent a total of 268 weeks at world No. 1, including 160 consecutive weeks (a record he held for 30 years before being overtaken by R.Federer in 2007).</center>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Weeks_at_No._1">Weeks at No. 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_ATP_number_1_ranked_singles_tennis_players&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Weeks at No. 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_player">By player</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_ATP_number_1_ranked_singles_tennis_players&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: By player">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The table on the left shows the total number of weeks that each player has been ranked No. 1 in their career by the ATP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_of_No._1_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_No._1-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The table on the right shows the number of consecutive weeks each player has been ranked No. 1 by the ATP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_of_No._1_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_No._1-7">[7]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Year-end_No._1">Year-end No. 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_ATP_number_1_ranked_singles_tennis_players&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Year-end No. 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The ATP year-end No. 1 ranked player is determined as the player at the head of the ATP rankings following the completion of the final tournament of the calendar year, usually in November or December. <a href="/wiki/Pete_Sampras" title="Pete Sampras">Pete Sampras</a> holds the record of six year-end No. 1 rankings, which were in consecutive years from 1993 through 1998.</p>
<p>Six players have stayed at ATP No. 1 in the rankings every week of a calendar year. Federer is the only player to have been ranked No. 1 every week for three consecutive calendar years.</p>
